nRhiJb-ObfsIf nRhiJb-fmcmS-oXtfBe"><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-c5RTEf"></div><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-qWD73c"><h5 class="cHE8Ub Qwf2Db-MnozTc Qwf2Db-MnozTc-OWXEXe-MnozTc-qWD73c">Mandiant </h5><p class="nRhiJb-qJTHM khCp7b"></p></div></section></div></section><div class="nRhiJb-DARUcf"><div class="nRhiJb-ObfsIf nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-ma6Yeb nRhiJb-DbgRPb-qWD73c-cGMI2b"><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-ibL1re dzoHJ"><div class="aLW4J" track-metadata-module="left rail"><h5 class="qZDXV Qwf2Db-MnozTc Qwf2Db-MnozTc-OWXEXe-MnozTc-wNfPc">Mandiant Incident Response</h5><p class="nRhiJb-cHYyed Mrfygc nRhiJb-BP2Omd-ma6Yeb-KE6vqe nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-cGMI2b">Investigate, contain, and remediate security incidents.</p><a class="nRhiJb-LgbsSe  nRhiJb-LgbsSe-OWXEXe-CNusmb-o6Shpd " href="https://cloud.google.com/security/consulting/mandiant-incident-response-services" track-metadata-module="left rail"track-metadata-module_headline="mandiant incident response" track-name="learn more"track-type="button"track-metadata-position="cta"track-metadata-eventdetail="cloud.google.com/security/consulting/mandiant-incident-response-services">Learn more </a></div></div><div class="OYL9D nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-OiUrBf" jsname="tx2NYc"><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Written by: Diana Ion, Rommel Joven, Yash Gupta</p>
<hr></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Since November 2024, </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/security/products/mandiant-managed-threat-hunting"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant Threat Defense</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> has been investigating an UNC6032 campaign that weaponizes the interest around AI tools, in particular those tools which can be used to generate videos based on user prompts. UNC6032 utilizes fake “AI video generator” websites to distribute malware leading to the deployment of payloads such as Python-based infostealers and several backdoors. Victims are typically directed to these fake websites via malicious social media ads that masquerade as legitimate AI video generator tools like Luma AI, Canva Dream Lab, and Kling AI, among others. Mandiant Threat Defense has identified thousands of UNC6032-linked ads that have collectively reached millions of users across various social media platforms like Facebook and LinkedIn. We suspect similar campaigns are active on other platforms as well, as cybercriminals consistently evolve tactics to evade detection and target multiple platforms to increase their chances of success. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant Threat Defense has observed UNC6032 compromises culminating in the exfiltration of login credentials, cookies, credit card data, and Facebook information through the Telegram API. This campaign has been active since at least mid-2024 and has impacted victims across different geographies and industries. Google Threat Intelligence Group (GTIG) assesses UNC6032 to have a Vietnam nexus. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant Threat Defense acknowledges Meta's collaborative and proactive threat hunting efforts in removing the identified malicious ads, domains, and accounts. Notably, a significant portion of Meta’s detection and removal began in 2024, prior to Mandiant alerting them of additional malicious activity we identified.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">A <a href="https://www.morphisec.com/blog/new-noodlophile-stealer-fake-ai-video-generation-platforms/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">similar investigation</a> was recently published by Morphisec</span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">.</span></span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Campaign Overview</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Threat actors haven't wasted a moment capitalizing on the global fascination with Artificial Intelligence. As AI's popularity surged over the past couple of years, cybercriminals quickly moved to exploit the widespread excitement. Their actions have fueled a massive and rapidly expanding campaign centered on fraudulent websites masquerading as cutting-edge AI tools. These websites have been promoted by a large network of misleading social media ads, similar to the ones shown in Figure 1 and Figure 2. </span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig1.max-2100x2100.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig1.max-2100x2100.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig1.max-2100x2100.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig1.max-2100x2100.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 1: Malicious Facebook ads</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig2.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig2.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig2.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig2.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 2: Malicious LinkedIn ads</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">As part of </span><a href="https://about.fb.com/news/2023/08/new-features-and-additional-transparency-measures-as-the-digital-services-act-comes-into-effect/" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Meta’s implementation of the Digital Services Act</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, the Ad Library displays additional information (ad campaign dates, targeting parameters and ad reach) on all ads that target people from the European Union. LinkedIn has also implemented a similar transparency tool.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Our research through both Ad Library tools identified over 30 different websites, mentioned across thousands of ads, active since mid 2024, all displaying similar ad content. The majority of ads which we found ran on Facebook, with only a handful also advertised on LinkedIn. The ads were published using both attacker-created Facebook pages, as well as by compromised Facebook accounts. Mandiant Threat Defense performed further analysis of a sample of over 120 malicious ads and, from the EU transparency section of the ads, their total reach for EU countries was over 2.3 million users. Table 1 displays the top 5 Facebook ads by reach. It should be noted that reach does not equate to the number of victims. </span><a href="https://www.facebook.com/business/help/710746785663278" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">According to Meta</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, the reach of an ad is an estimated number of how many Account Center accounts saw the ad at least once. </span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><div align="left" style="text-align:center">

<span style="color:#5f6368;display:block;font-size:16px;font-style:italic;margin-top:8px;width:100%"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Table 1: Top 5 Facebook ads by reach</span></span></div></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The threat actor constantly rotates the domains mentioned in the Facebook ads, likely to avoid detection and account bans. We noted that once a domain is registered, it will be referenced in ads within a few days if not the same day. Moreover, most of the ads are short lived, with new ones being created on a daily basis. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">On LinkedIn, we identified roughly 10 malicious ads, each directing users to </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">hxxps://klingxai[.]com</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. This domain was registered on September 19, 2024, and the first ad appeared just a day later. These ads have a total impression estimate of 50k-250k. For each ad, the United States was the region with the highest percentage of impressions, although the targeting included other regions such as Europe and Australia.</span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><div align="center">

<span style="color:#5f6368;display:block;font-size:16px;font-style:italic;margin-top:8px;width:100%">Table 2: LinkedIn ads</span></div></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">From the websites investigated, Mandiant Threat Defense observed that they have similar interfaces and offer purported functionalities such as text-to-video or image-to-video generation. Once the user provides a prompt to generate a video, regardless of the input, the website will serve one of the static payloads hosted on the same (or related) infrastructure. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The payload downloaded is the STARKVEIL malware. It drops three different modular malware families, primarily designed for information theft and capable of downloading plugins to extend their functionality. The presence of multiple, similar payloads suggests a fail-safe mechanism, allowing the attack to persist even if some payloads are detected or blocked by security defences.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In the next section, we will delve deeper into one particular compromise Mandiant Threat Defense responded to.</span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Luma AI Investigation</span></h2>
<h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Infection Chain</span></h3></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig3.max-2100x2100.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig3.max-2100x2100.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig3.max-2100x2100.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig3.max-2100x2100.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 3: Infection chain lifecycle</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">This blog post provides a detailed analysis of our findings on the key components of this campaign:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Lure: </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The threat actors leverage social networks to push AI-themed ads that direct users to fake AI websites, resulting in malware downloads.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Malware</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: It contains several malware components, including the STARKVEIL dropper, which deploys the XWORM and FROSTRIFT backdoors and the GRIMPULL downloader.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Execution</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: The malware makes extensive use of DLL side-loading, in-memory droppers, and process injection to execute its payloads.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Persistence</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: It uses AutoRun registry key for its two Backdoors (XWORM and FROSTRIFT).</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Anti-VM and Anti-analysis</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: GRIMPULL checks for commonly used artifacts\features from known Sandbox and analysis tools.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Reconnaissance</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> </span></p>
</li>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:circle;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Host reconnaissance</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: XWORM and FROSTRIFT survey the host by collecting information, including OS, username, role, hardware identifiers, and installed AV.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:circle;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Software reconnaissance</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: FROSTRIFT checks the existence of certain messaging applications and browsers.</span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Command-and-control (C2)</strong></p>
</li>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:circle;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Tor</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: GRIMPULL utilizes a Tor Tunnel to fetch additional .NET payloads.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:circle;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Telegram</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: XWORM sends victim notification via telegram including information gathered during host reconnaissance.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:circle;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">TCP</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: The malware connects to its C2 using ports 7789, 25699</span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, </span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">56001.</span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Information stealer </strong></p>
</li>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:circle;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Keylogger</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: XWORM log keystrokes from the host.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:circle;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Browser extensions</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: FROSTRIFT scans for 48 browser extensions related to Password managers, Authenticators, and Digital wallets potentially for data theft.</span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Backdoor Commands</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: XWORM supports multiple commands for further compromise.</span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The Lure</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">This particular case began from a Facebook Ad for “Luma Dream AI Machine”, masquerading as a well-known text-to-video AI tool - Luma AI. The ad, as seen in Figure 4, redirected the user to an attacker-created website hosted at </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">hxxps://lumalabsai[.]in/.</code></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig4.max-1300x1300.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig4.max-1300x1300.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig4.max-1300x1300.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig4.max-1300x1300.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 4: The ad the victim clicked on</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Once on the fake Luma AI website, the user can click the “Start Free Now” button and choose from various video generation functionalities. Regardless of the selected option, the same prompt is displayed, as shown in the GIF in Figure 5. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">This multi-step process, made to resemble any other legitimate text-to-video or image-to-video generation tool website, creates a sense of familiarity to the user and does not give any immediate indication of malicious intent. Once the user hits the generate button, a loading bar appears, mimicking an AI model hard at work. After a few seconds, when the new video is supposedly ready, a Download button is displayed. This leads to the download of a ZIP archive file on the victim host.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/original_images/fake-ai-fig5a.gif" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/original_images/fake-ai-fig5a.gif" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/original_images/fake-ai-fig5a.gif" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/original_images/fake-ai-fig5a.gif" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 5: Fake AI video generation website</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Unsurprisingly, the ready-to-download archive is one of many payloads already hosted on the same server, with no connection to the user input. In this case, several archives were hosted at the path </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">hxxps://lumalabsai[.]in/complete/</code>. <span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant determined that the website will serve the archive file with the most recent “Last Modified” value, indicating continuous updates by the threat actor. Mandiant compared some of these payloads and found them to be functionally similar, with different obfuscation techniques applied, thus resulting in different sizes.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig6.max-1200x1200.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig6.max-1200x1200.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig6.max-1200x1200.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig6.max-1200x1200.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 6: Payloads hosted at hxxps://lumalabsai[.]in/complete</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Execution</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The previously downloaded ZIP archive contains an executable with a double extension (</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">.mp4</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and</span> <code style="vertical-align:baseline">.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">) in its name, separated by thirteen </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">Braille Pattern Blank (Unicode: U+2800, UTF-8: E2 A0 80)</code> <span style="vertical-align:baseline">characters. This is a special whitespace character from the Braille Pattern Block in Unicode.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig7a.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig7a.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig7a.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig7a.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 7: Braille Pattern Blank characters in the file name</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The resulting file name, </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">Lumalabs_1926326251082123689-626.mp4⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, aims to make the binary less suspicious by pushing the</span> <code style="vertical-align:baseline">.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> extension out of the user view. The number of Braille Pattern Blank characters used varies across different samples served, ranging from 13 to more than 30. To further hide the true purpose of this binary, the default </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">.mp4</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> Windows icon is used on the malicious file.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Figure 8 shows how the file looks on Windows 11, compared to a legitimate</span> <code style="vertical-align:baseline">.mp4</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> file.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig8.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig8.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig8.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig8.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 8: Malicious binary vs legitimate .mp4 file</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">STARKVEIL</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The binary </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">Lumalabs_1926326251082123689-626.mp4⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, tracked by Mandiant as STARKVEIL</span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">,</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> is a dropper written in Rust. Once executed, it extracts an embedded archive containing benign executables and its malware components. These are later utilized to inject malicious code into several legitimate processes. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Executing the malware displays an error window, as seen in Figure 9, to trick the user into trying to execute it again and into believing that the file is corrupted.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH H05fDc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig9.max-400x400.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig9.max-400x400.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH H05fDc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig9.max-400x400.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig9.max-400x400.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 9: Error window displayed when executing STARKVEIL</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">For a successful compromise, the executable needs to run twice; the initial execution results in the extraction of all the embedded files under the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">C:\winsystem\</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> directory.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig10.max-1400x1400.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig10.max-1400x1400.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig10.max-1400x1400.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig10.max-1400x1400.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 10: Files in the winsystem directory</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">During the second execution, the main executable spawns the Python Launcher, </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">py.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, with an obfuscated Python command as an argument. The Python command decodes an embedded Python code, which Mandiant tracks as COILHATCH</span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline"> </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">dropper. COILHATCH performs the following actions (note that the script has been deobfuscated and renamed for improved readability):</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The command takes a </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">Base85</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">-encoded string, decodes it, decompresses the result using </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">zlib</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, deserializes the resulting data using the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">marshal</code><strong style="vertical-align:baseline"> </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">module, and then executes the final deserialized data as Python code.</span></li>
</ul></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig11a.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig11a.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig11a.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig11a.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 11: Python command</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><ul>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The decompiled first-stage Python code combines </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">RSA</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">AES</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">RC4</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, and </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">XOR</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> techniques to decrypt the second stage Python bytecode.</span></li>
</ul></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig12.max-1500x1500.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig12.max-1500x1500.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig12.max-1500x1500.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig12.max-1500x1500.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 12: First-stage Python</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><ul>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The decrypted second-stage Python script executes </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">C:\winsystem\heif\heif.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, which is a legitimate, digitally signed executable, used to side-load a malicious DLL. This serves as the launcher to execute the other malware components.</span></li>
</ul></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig13a.max-700x700.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig13a.max-700x700.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig13a.max-700x700.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig13a.max-700x700.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 13: Second-stage Python</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>The following is the resulting process tree:</p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><pre><code>explorer.exe 
  ↳ 7zfm.exe &quot;&lt;path&gt;\Lumalabs_1926326251082123689-626.zip&quot;
    ↳ &quot;&lt;path&gt;\lumalabs_1926326251082123689-626.mp4⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀.exe&quot; 
      ↳ &quot;C:\winsystem\py\py.exe&quot; -c exec(__import__ ..&lt;ENCODED PYTHON CODE&gt;..) 
         ↳ &quot;C:\WINDOWS\system32\cmd.exe&quot; /c &quot;C:\winsystem\heif\heif.exe&quot;
           ↳ &quot;C:\winsystem\heif\heif.exe&quot;</code></pre></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Malware Analysis</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">As mentioned, the STARKVEIL malware drops its components during its first execution and executes a launcher on its second execution. <span style="color:#5f6368;display:block;font-size:16px;font-style:italic;margin-top:8px;width:100%">Table 3: Malware components</span></div></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Each of these DLLs operates as an in-memory dropper and spawns a new victim process to perform code injection through process replacement.</span></p>
<h4><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Launcher</span></h4>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The execution of </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">C:\winsystem\heif\heif.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> results in the side-loading of the malicious </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">heif.dll</code><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">, </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">located in the</span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline"> </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">same directory. This DLL is an in-memory dropper that spawns a legitimate Windows process (which may vary) and performs code injection through process replacement.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The injected code is a .NET executable that acts as a launcher and performs the following:</span></p>
<ol>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Moves multiple folders from </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">C:\winsystem</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. The destination folders are:</span>
<ul>
<li><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%\python</code></li>
<li><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%\pythonw</code></li>
<li><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%\ffplay</code></li>
<li><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%\Launcher</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Launches three legitimate processes to side-load associated malicious DLLs. The malicious DLLs for each process are:
<ul>
<li><code style="vertical-align:baseline">python.exe: %APPDATA%\python\avcodec-61.dll </code></li>
<li><code style="vertical-align:baseline">pythonw.exe: %APPDATA%\pythonw\heif.dll </code></li>
<li><code style="vertical-align:baseline">ffplay.exe: %APPDATA%\ffplay\libde265.dll</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Establishes persistence via AutoRun registry key.
<ul>
<li><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">value</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: Dropbox</span></li>
<li><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">key</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run\</span></li>
<li><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">root</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: HKCU\</span></li>
<li><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">value data</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">&quot;cmd.exe /c \&quot;cd /d &quot;&lt;exePath&gt;&quot; &amp;&amp; &quot;Launcher.exe&quot;&quot;</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ol></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig14.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig14.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig14.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig14.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 14: Main function of launcher</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The AutoRun Key executes </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%\Launcher\Launcher.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> that sideloads the DLL file </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">libde265.dll</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. This DLL spawns and injects its payload into </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">AddInProcess32.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> via PE hollowing. The injected code’s main purpose is to execute the legitimate binaries </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">C:\winsystem\heif2rgb\heif2rgb.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">C:\winsystem\heif-info\heif-info.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, which, in turn, sideload the backdoors XWORM and FROSTRIFT,</span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline"> </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">respectively.</span></p>
<h4><span style="vertical-align:baseline">GRIMPULL</span></h4>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Of the three executables, the launcher first executes </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%\python\python.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, which side-loads the DLL </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">avcodec-61.dll</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and injects the malware GRIMPULL</span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline"> </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">into a legitimate Windows process. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">GRIMPULL</span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline"> </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">is a .NET-based downloader that incorporates anti-VM capabilities and utilizes </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">Tor</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> for C2 server connections.</span></p>
<h5><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Anti-VM and Anti-Analysis </span></h5>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">GRIMPULL begins by checking for the presence of the mutex value </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">aff391c406ebc4c3</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, and terminates itself if this is found. Otherwise, the malware proceeds to perform further anti-VM checks, exiting in case any of the mentioned checks succeeds.</span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><div align="center">

<span style="color:#5f6368;display:block;font-size:16px;font-style:italic;margin-top:8px;width:100%">Table 4: <span style="vertical-align:baseline">Anti-VM and Anti-analysis checks</span></span></div></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h5><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Download Function</span></h5>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">GRIMPULL</span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline"> </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">verifies the presence of a Tor process. If a Tor process is not detected, it proceeds to download, decompress, and execute Tor from the following URL:</span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><pre><code>https://archive.torproject.org/tor-package-archive/torbrowser/13.0.9/
tor-expert-bundle-windows-i686-13.0.9.tar.gz</code></pre></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig15.max-1300x1300.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig15.max-1300x1300.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig15.max-1300x1300.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig15.max-1300x1300.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 15: Download function</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Afterwards, Tor will run locally on port </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">9050</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">.</span></p>
<h5><span style="vertical-align:baseline">C2 Communication</span></h5>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">GRIMPULL then attempts to connect to the following C2 server via the Tor tunnel over TCP.</span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><pre><code>strokes[.]zapto[.]org:7789</code></pre></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The malware maintains this connection and periodically checks for .NET payloads. Fetched payloads are decrypted using </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">TripleDES</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> in ECB mode with the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">MD5</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> hash of the campaign ID </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">aff391c406ebc4c3</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> as the decryption key, decompressed with </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">GZip</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> (using a 4-byte length prefix), reversed, and then loaded into memory as .NET assemblies.</span></p>
<h5><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Malware Configuration</span></h5>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The configuration elements are encoded as </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">base64</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> strings, as shown in Figure 16.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig16.max-700x700.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig16.max-700x700.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig16.max-700x700.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig16.max-700x700.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 16: Encoded malware configuration</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Table 5 shows the extracted malware configuration.</span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><div align="center">

Table 5: GRIMPULL configuration</div></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h4><span style="vertical-align:baseline">XWORM</span></h4>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Secondly, the launcher executes the file </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%\pythonw\pythonw.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, which side-loads the DLL </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">heif.dll</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and injects XWORM into a legitimate Windows process.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">XWORM is a .NET-based backdoor that communicates using a custom binary protocol over TCP. Its core functionality involves expanding its capabilities through a plugin management system. Downloaded plugins are written to disk and executed. Supported capabilities include keylogging, command execution, screen capture, and spreading to USB drives.</span></p>
<h5><span style="vertical-align:baseline">XWORM Configuration</span></h5>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The malware begins by decoding its configuration using the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">AES</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> algorithm.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig17.max-1000x1000.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig17.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig17.max-1000x1000.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig17.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 17: Decryption of configuration</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Table 6 shows the extracted malware configuration.</span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><div align="center">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">

<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">

<span style="color:#5f6368;display:block;font-size:16px;font-style:italic;margin-top:8px;width:100%">Table 7: Supported commands</span></div></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h4><span style="vertical-align:baseline">FROSTRIFT</span></h4>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Lastly, the </span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">l</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">auncher executes the file </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%\ffplay\ffplay.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to side-load the DLL </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%\ffplay\libde265.dll</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and inject FROSTRIFT into a legitimate Windows process.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">FROSTRIFT is a .NET backdoor that collects system information, installed applications, and crypto wallets. Instead of receiving C2 commands, it receives .NET modules that are stored in the registry to be loaded in-memory. It communicates with the C2 server using </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">GZIP</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">-compressed </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">protobuf</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> messages over TCP/SSL.</span></p>
<h5><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Malware Configuration</span></h5>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The malware starts by decoding its configuration, which is a Base64-encoded and GZIP-compressed protobuf message embedded within the strings table.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig18.max-1100x1100.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig18.max-1100x1100.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig18.max-1100x1100.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig18.max-1100x1100.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 18: FROSTRIFT configuration</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Table 8 shows the extracted malware configuration.</span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><div align="center">

<span style="color:#5f6368;display:block;font-size:16px;font-style:italic;margin-top:8px;width:100%">Table 8: FROSTRIFT configration</span></div></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h5><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Persistence</span></h5>
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">FROSTRIFT</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> can achieve persistence by running the command:</span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><pre><code>powershell.exe &quot;Remove-ItemProperty -Path &#39;HKCU:\SOFTWARE\
Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run&#39; -Name &#39;&lt;sample_file_name&gt;
&#39;;New-ItemProperty -Path &#39;HKCU:\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\
CurrentVersion\Run&#39; -Name &#39;&lt;sample_file_name&gt;&#39; -Value &#39;&quot;&quot;%APPDATA%
\&lt;sample_file_name&gt;&quot;&quot;&#39; -PropertyType &#39;String&#39;&quot;</code></pre></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The sample copies itself to </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">%APPDATA%</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and adds a new registry value under </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">HKCU\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> with the new file path as data to ensure persistence at each system startup.</span></p>

<span style="color:#5f6368;display:block;font-size:16px;font-style:italic;margin-top:8px;width:100%">Table 11: List of browser extensions</span></div></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h5><span style="vertical-align:baseline">C2 Communication </span></h5>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The malware expects the C2 to respond by sending </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">GZIP</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">-compressed Protobuf messages with the following fields:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><code style="vertical-align:baseline">registry_val</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: A registry value under </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">HKCU\Software\&lt;victim_id&gt;</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to store the loader_bytes.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><code style="vertical-align:baseline">loader_bytes</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: Assembly module to load the loaded_bytes (stored at registry in reverse order).</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><code style="vertical-align:baseline">loaded_bytes</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: GZIP-compressed assembly module to be loaded in-memory.</span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The sample receives </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">loader_bytes</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> only in the first message as it stores it under the registry value </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">HKCU\Software\&lt;victim_id&gt;\registry_val</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. For the subsequent messages, it only receives </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">registry_val</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> which it uses to fetch </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">loader_bytes</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> from the registry.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The sample sends empty </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">GZIP</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">-compressed Protobuf messages as a keep-alive mechanism until the C2 sends another assembly module to be loaded.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The malware has the ability to download and execute extra payloads from the following hardcoded URLs (this feature is not enabled in this sample):</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><code style="vertical-align:baseline">WebDriver2.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: hxxps://github[.]com/DFfe9ewf/test3/raw/refs/heads/main/WebDriver.dll;</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><code style="vertical-align:baseline">chromedriver2.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: hxxps://github[.]com/DFfe9ewf/test3/raw/refs/heads/main/chromedriver.exe</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><code style="vertical-align:baseline">msedgedriver2.exe</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: hxxps://github[.]com/DFfe9ewf/test3/raw/refs/heads/main/msedgedriver.exe</span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The files are WebDrivers for browsers that can be used for testing, automation, and interacting with the browser. They can also be used by attackers for malicious purposes, such as deploying additional payloads.</span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Conclusion</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">As AI has gained tremendous momentum recently, our research highlights some of the ways in which threat actors have taken advantage of it. Although our investigation was limited in scope, we discovered that well-crafted fake “AI websites” pose a significant threat to both organizations and individual users. These AI tools no longer target just graphic designers; anyone can be lured in by a seemingly harmless ad. The temptation to try the latest AI tool can lead to anyone becoming a victim. We advise users to exercise caution when engaging with AI tools and to verify the legitimacy of the website's domain. </span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Acknowledgements</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Special thanks to Stephen Eckels, Muhammad Umair, and Mustafa Nasser for their assistance in analyzing the malware samples. Richmond Liclican for his inputs and attribution. Ervin Ocampo, Swapnil Patil, Muhammad Umer Khan, and Muhammad Hasib Latif for providing the detection opportunities.</span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Detection Opportunities</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The following indicators of compromise (IOCs) and YARA rules are also available as a </span><a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/504d3096e03ec01eeb3b6c7a5bc3a57bf44c85b85bcce5a3297e087ebc53c151" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">collection</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and rule pack in Google Threat Intelligence (GTI). </span></p>

	meta:
		author = "Mandiant"
	strings:
		$i1 = "zlib.decompress" ascii wide
		$i2 = "rc4" ascii wide
		$i3 = "aes_decrypt" ascii wide
		$i4 = "xor" ascii wide
		$i5 = "rsa_decrypt" ascii wide
		$r1 = "private_key" ascii wide
		$r2 = "runner" ascii wide
		$r3 = "marshal" ascii wide
		$r4 = "marshal.loads" ascii wide
		$r5 = "b85decode" ascii wide
		$r6 = "exceute_func" ascii wide
		$r7 = "hybrid_decrypt" ascii wide
	condition:
		(4 of ($i*)) and all of ($r*)
}</code></pre></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><pre><code>rule G_Dropper_STARKVEIL_1 {
	meta:
		author = "Mandiant"
	strings:
		$p00_0 = { 56 57 53 48 83 EC ?? 48 8D AA [4] 48 8B 7D 
?? 48 8B 4F ?? FF 15 [4] 48 89 F9 }
		$p00_1 = { 0F 0B 66 0F 1F 84 00 [4] 48 89 54 24 ?? 55 41 
56 56 57 53 48 83 EC }
	condition:
		uint16(0) == 0x5A4D and uint32(uint32(0x3C)) == 0x00004550 
and (($p00_0 in (48000 .. 59000) and $p00_1 in (100000 .. 120000)))
}</code></pre></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><pre><code>import "dotnet"

rule G_Downloader_GRIMPULL_1 {
	meta:
		author = "Mandiant"
	strings:
		$str1 = "SbieDll.dll" ascii wide
		$str2 = "cuckoomon.dll" ascii wide

		$str5 = "VMware|VIRTUAL|A M I|Xen" ascii wide
		$str6 = "Microsoft|VMWare|Virtual" ascii wide
		$str7 = "win32_process.handle='{0}'" ascii wide
		$str8 = "stealer" ascii wide

	condition:
		dotnet.is_dotnet and all of them
}</code></pre></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><pre><code>rule G_Backdoor_FROSTRIFT_1 {

		author = "Mandiant"
	strings:
		$guid = "$23e83ead-ecb2-418f-9450-813fb7da66b8"
		$r1 = "IdentifiableDecryptor.DecryptorStack"
		$r2 = "$ProtoBuf.Explorers.ExplorerDecryptor"

		$s4 = "SELECT * FROM Win32_PnPEntity WHERE (PNPClass = 
'Image' OR PNPClass = 'Camera')" wide

		$s6 = "Bitcoin-Qt" wide
	condition:
		uint16(0) == 0x5a4d and (all of ($s*) or $guid or all of ($r*))
}</code></pre></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">YARA-L Rules</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant has made the relevant rules available in the Google SecOps Mandiant Intel Emerging Threats </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/chronicle/docs/detection/curated-detections"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">curated detections</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> rule set. The activity discussed in the blog post is detected under the rule names:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Suspicious Binary File Execution - MP4 Masquerade</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Suspicious Binary File Execution - Double Extension and Braille Pattern Blank Masquerade</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Python Script Deobfuscation - Base85 ZLib Marshal</span></p>

Intelligence\"],\"timeRequired\":\"PT53M\"}\u003c/script\u003e"],["Text-to-Malware: How Cybercriminals Weaponize Fake AI-Themed Websites"],null,null,[[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003eWritten by: Diana Ion, Rommel Joven, Yash Gupta\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003chr\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSince November 2024, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://cloud.google.com/security/products/mandiant-managed-threat-hunting\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eMandiant Threat Defense\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e has been investigating an UNC6032 campaign that weaponizes the interest around AI tools, in particular those tools which can be used to generate videos based on user prompts. UNC6032 utilizes fake “AI video generator” websites to distribute malware leading to the deployment of payloads such as Python-based infostealers and several backdoors. Victims are typically directed to these fake websites via malicious social media ads that masquerade as legitimate AI video generator tools like Luma AI, Canva Dream Lab, and Kling AI, among others. Mandiant Threat Defense has identified thousands of UNC6032-linked ads that have collectively reached millions of users across various social media platforms like Facebook and LinkedIn. We suspect similar campaigns are active on other platforms as well, as cybercriminals consistently evolve tactics to evade detection and target multiple platforms to increase their chances of success. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eMandiant Threat Defense has observed UNC6032 compromises culminating in the exfiltration of login credentials, cookies, credit card data, and Facebook information through the Telegram API. This campaign has been active since at least mid-2024 and has impacted victims across different geographies and industries. Google Threat Intelligence Group (GTIG) assesses UNC6032 to have a Vietnam nexus. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eMandiant Threat Defense acknowledges Meta's collaborative and proactive threat hunting efforts in removing the identified malicious ads, domains, and accounts. Notably, a significant portion of Meta’s detection and removal began in 2024, prior to Mandiant alerting them of additional malicious activity we identified.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eA \u003ca href\u003d\"https://www.morphisec.com/blog/new-noodlophile-stealer-fake-ai-video-generation-platforms/\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003esimilar investigation\u003c/a\u003e was recently published by Morphisec\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eCampaign Overview\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThreat actors haven't wasted a moment capitalizing on the global fascination with Artificial Intelligence. As AI's popularity surged over the past couple of years, cybercriminals quickly moved to exploit the widespread excitement. Their actions have fueled a massive and rapidly expanding campaign centered on fraudulent websites masquerading as cutting-edge AI tools. These websites have been promoted by a large network of misleading social media ads, similar to the ones shown in Figure 1 and Figure 2. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 1: Malicious Facebook ads\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig1.max-2100x2100.png","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig1.max-1100x1100.png 1060w, https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig1.max-2100x2100.png 2007w"," 1060px,  2007px","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig1.max-2100x2100.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 2: Malicious LinkedIn ads\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig2.max-900x900.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/fake-ai-fig2.max-900x900.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAs part of \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://about.fb.com/news/2023/08/new-features-and-additional-transparency-measures-as-the-digital-services-act-comes-into-effect/\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eMeta’s implementation of the Digital Services Act\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e, the Ad Library displays additional information (ad campaign dates, targeting parameters and ad reach) on all ads that target people from the European Union. LinkedIn has also implemented a similar transparency tool.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eOur research through both Ad Library tools identified over 30 different websites, mentioned across thousands of ads, active since mid 2024, all displaying similar ad content. The majority of ads which we found ran on Facebook, with only a handful also advertised on LinkedIn. The ads were published using both attacker-created Facebook pages, as well as by compromised Facebook accounts. Mandiant Threat Defense performed further analysis of a sample of over 120 malicious ads and, from the EU transparency section of the ads, their total reach for EU countries was over 2.3 million users. Table 1 displays the top 5 Facebook ads by reach. It should be noted that reach does not equate to the number of victims. \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://www.facebook.com/business/help/710746785663278\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAccording to Meta\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e, the reach of an ad is an estimated number of how many Account Center accounts saw the ad at least once. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cdiv align\u003d\"left\" style\u003d\"text-align:center\"\u003e\n\u003cdiv Although our investigation was limited in scope, we discovered that well-crafted fake “AI websites” pose a significant threat to both organizations and individual users. These AI tools no longer target just graphic designers; anyone can be lured in by a seemingly harmless ad. The temptation to try the latest AI tool can lead to anyone becoming a victim. We advise users to exercise caution when engaging with AI tools and to verify the legitimacy of the website's domain. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAcknowledgements\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSpecial thanks to Stephen Eckels, Muhammad Umair, and Mustafa Nasser for their assistance in analyzing the malware samples. Richmond Liclican for his inputs and attribution.
